<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_1dccf5d5-c034-45ff-b429-f998a9070822'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>
</script>

  <span id="freeText12734893457160318630" style="display:none">When Rohan became the new prince of the Desert, ruler of the kingdom granted to his family for as long as the Long Sands spewed fire, he took the crown with two goals in mind. First and foremost, he sought to bring permanent peace to his world of divided princedoms. And, in a land where dragon-slaying was a proof of manhood, Rohan was the sole champion of the dragons, fighting desperately to preserve the last remaining lords of the sky and with them a secret which might be the salvation of his people....<br /> <br />Sioned, the Sunrunner witch who was fated by Fire to be Rohanâ€™s bride, had mastered the magic of sunlight and moonglow, catching hints of a yet to be formed pattern which could irrevocably affect the destinies of Sunrunners and ordinary mortals alike. Yet caught in the machinations of the Lady of Goddess Keep, and of Prince Rohan and his sworn enemy, the treacherously cunning High Prince, could Sioned alter this crucial pattern to protect her lord from the menace of a war that threatened to set the land ablaze?</span>

<div id="review_304992291" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/304992291" />
    <a title="Zackery Arbela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7743547-zackery-arbela"><img alt="Zackery Arbela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442622674p2/7743547.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/304992291?book_show_action=true">Apr 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zackery Arbela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zackery Arbela" href="/user/show/7743547-zackery-arbela">Zackery Arbela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer304992291" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17480466692459247598">Gather round children, and cast your minds back to the ye old days of the late 80's/early 90's, when fantasy was still very much an underground thing, most stories were tedious Tolkien retreads or Dungeons and Dragons sessions put down on paper, and writers of the feminine persuasion were notably light on the ground. Which makes this book and the various series it spawn so interesting....<br/><br/>Nowadays, female fantasy authors are a pretty common sight, so it's a bit shocking to consider just how ahead</span>
  <span id="freeText17480466692459247598" style="display:none">Gather round children, and cast your minds back to the ye old days of the late 80's/early 90's, when fantasy was still very much an underground thing, most stories were tedious Tolkien retreads or Dungeons and Dragons sessions put down on paper, and writers of the feminine persuasion were notably light on the ground. Which makes this book and the various series it spawn so interesting....<br /><br />Nowadays, female fantasy authors are a pretty common sight, so it's a bit shocking to consider just how ahead of its time Dragon Prince was in terms of what could be done in a traditional fantasy novel. When I first picked it up, it was amazed just how different this was from the other fare to be found in bookstores (yes, books were sold in actual stores. Ask your Dad....)What Melanie Rawn did with this story was take all the elements of an awesome epic fantasy and mix it with the conventions of a romance novel, seasoned with some of the most detailed and compelling examples of world building to be found anywhere. The result was something groundbreaking. While there are battles galore and fantastical deed by the score, the core of this tale is the relationship between Rohan and Sioned, the passion that draws them together, the dangers and obstacles that block them. No final voyages to Valhalla here...more along the lines of a traditional romance, Lancelot and Guinevere, Romeo and Juliet, or any number of bodice rippers sold by the dozen made magnificent by the inclusion of dragons.<br /><br />Today it's a common enough formula, which makes this book something of a groundbreaker. It showed (to angsty Gen-X teenagers at least) that fantasy could be more than just the slay the dragon while standing on a mountain of skulls. That there was room for real emotion and passion.<br /><br />In short, a good read. Not to mention the cover art by Michael Whelan, reason enough to buy the printed version.<br />Posted by Zackery Arbela </span>
  <a data-text-id="17480466692459247598" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1264392356" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1264392356" />
    <a title="Wyrdness" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16477808-wyrdness"><img alt="Wyrdness" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1264392356?book_show_action=true">Apr 25, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wyrdness" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wyrdness" href="/user/show/16477808-wyrdness">Wyrdness</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8217075-dragon-prince">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16477808-wyrdness?shelf=lets-forget-this-happened">lets-forget-this-happened</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16477808-wyrdness?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16477808-wyrdness?shelf=shelf-of-awful">shelf-of-awful</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1264392356" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7706198597911012409">I feel rather betrayed by one of my favourite authors (Grace Draven) giving this 5 stars. I can understand why she likes it so much, it is well written and manages to weave several character threads in to an involved story without giving too much focus to any one in particular. Yet I found myself disliking most of the characters by the end of the novel and for me personally that always leads to a bad rating. Add that to the problems I had with the events near the end of the book and, well, it wa</span>
  <span id="freeText7706198597911012409" style="display:none">I feel rather betrayed by one of my favourite authors (Grace Draven) giving this 5 stars. I can understand why she likes it so much, it is well written and manages to weave several character threads in to an involved story without giving too much focus to any one in particular. Yet I found myself disliking most of the characters by the end of the novel and for me personally that always leads to a bad rating. Add that to the problems I had with the events near the end of the book and, well, it was not going to end well...<br /><br />For me this book was going quite well up until somewhere around the 70% mark, then it fell over a cliff and never managed to redeem itself in my eyes. Up until that point I'd been enjoying the (not so subtle) intrigues and how the characters felt like they truly influenced events around them, but I'm sorry, the entire concept of one of the protagonists I'm supposed to be sympathetic to hate-raping the daughter of his enemy is a massive big read X for me. Nope, just no, I am done. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[This goes double when the hate-rape involves the character also cheating on a wife they're supposed to be deeply in love with and utterly devoted to all so they can father an "heir of the body". Especially when the same character not long previously rejected taking a mistress solely to have an heir because they said it wasn't a big deal and was utterly repulsed at the thought of having sex with anyone but said wife, and has up to this point been an honourable and idealistic individual.<br /><br />The fact that the wife was so remarkably calm about her husbands actions and even planned the murder of the (admittedly pretty horrible) mother and to raise his bastard son as her own was another WTF-I-am-done moment. I forgot to mention this is after her husband tried to rape her in an "I have no idea what's going on anymore" scene.<br /><br />All this hypocrisy and descent in to barbarism seems to be because they assume the wife is barren, yet they're both under 30 (in a world where people are still sprightly enough to kill dragons at 60), have only been married 6 years, and I would say 3 miscarriages (with one of those being from surviving a lethal plague) and her not being pregnant under severely stressful circumstances (in a harsh and unforgiving desert environment) is not really concrete proof of anything. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The amount of character twisting involved in these events completely robbed me of any enjoyment I was having, which is really a shame because I otherwise very much liked the world this was set in.<br /><br />If you are unbothered by rape-y bits and can overlook the hypocrisy of the main characters becoming just like the evil, abusive enemy they fight so hard against (which could have been cool if it showed any signs of being intentionally done), then perhaps you will enjoy this more than I did. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7706198597911012409" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_12019632" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/12019632" />
    <a title="Rachel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56210-rachel"><img alt="Rachel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1232489587p2/56210.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/12019632?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel" href="/user/show/56210-rachel">Rachel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People enjoying depraved acts and suchlike</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Rachel by: </span>
      nobody
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56210-rachel?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56210-rachel?shelf=love">love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56210-rachel?shelf=worst">worst</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer12019632" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15997911024277112774">Back in the 90s, I was helping by volunteering to set up a book sale at the local library with my mom. We also got first pick of the books there. I saw these books and they had nice covers, and an intriguing back. I asked my mom if I could buy them (being young myself). Ironically, it was from the box(es) of books we'd donated! And so, we bought back our own books, so that I could read them. (My mom swore she'd never donate books without running them by me first again.. not sure if she's held to</span>
  <span id="freeText15997911024277112774" style="display:none">Back in the 90s, I was helping by volunteering to set up a book sale at the local library with my mom. We also got first pick of the books there. I saw these books and they had nice covers, and an intriguing back. I asked my mom if I could buy them (being young myself). Ironically, it was from the box(es) of books we'd donated! And so, we bought back our own books, so that I could read them. (My mom swore she'd never donate books without running them by me first again.. not sure if she's held to that. But anyways.)<br /> If only I'd listened to my mother (she'd advised against reading it). I suppose the clue should have been that she'd donated it, when usually we kept them (and owned 500+ books). <br /> But lo, I read them. As much as I could stomach, anyways. Melanie Rawn has to be one of the trashiest, most vile book writers I've ever had the misfortune to read. I am not talking about her writing style, or even her wordplay. I'm talking about her ideas, and her views and portrayals of humanity - even her so-called "brightest" are people I'd never want to meet. If I could scrub her books from my mind I would. Pol, I'd thrash you and maybe worse if I ever met you. Among other people.<br />In her defense, some of the worst scenes are so artfully awful that they are imprinted on my memory - not many authors can do that. And to have me hating her over a decade later, speaks volumes of how solid, how real, the scenes she evokes are. And if I had stopped after reading the first half of the book (It's split into 2 stories), I could have thought much much more highly of her. Suffice to say, unless you like rather despicable people, acts, and such, don't read this book. Or the series.<br /><br />If you do, go right ahead.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15997911024277112774" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5812444855977246010">One of my favorite series. Owes quite a bit to <i>Dune</i>, I think, but creative enough on its own merits. In series like this, you often get either great characters or great plotting, but this has both. Heroes with dark sides, villains with layers, love and family and politics and magic twine together to keep your interest through several generations.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_150106188" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/150106188" />
    <a title="Terri" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3937614-terri"><img alt="Terri" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1377129083p2/3937614.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/150106188?book_show_action=true">Feb 23, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Terri" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Terri" href="/user/show/3937614-terri">Terri</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3937614-terri?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3937614-terri?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3937614-terri?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3937614-terri?shelf=dragons">dragons</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer150106188" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4121924579963675676">The story is very political, which is fine and normal in fantasy literature. It was the characters who disappointed me. Rohan's first few chapters introduced him as smart, capable and calculated. He wanted more for his kingdom than constant war, and seemed set to be a great literary hero. Unfortunately, his love for Sioned was not so beautiful. Like most of her male characters, Rohan's carnal urges overwhelmed his reason throughout the entire novel. His lust, or "Fire," for Sioned (and hers for </span>
  <span id="freeText4121924579963675676" style="display:none">The story is very political, which is fine and normal in fantasy literature. It was the characters who disappointed me. Rohan's first few chapters introduced him as smart, capable and calculated. He wanted more for his kingdom than constant war, and seemed set to be a great literary hero. Unfortunately, his love for Sioned was not so beautiful. Like most of her male characters, Rohan's carnal urges overwhelmed his reason throughout the entire novel. His lust, or "Fire," for Sioned (and hers for him) seemed to be the driving factor in their relationship. Only a few times in the book did the characters think fond thoughts of each other that had nothing to do with their sexual relationship. That's fine and good for a married couple, but their relationship should have been based on more than sex. At the end of the book, I still don't really feel I know the characters and more worrisome, I don't like what I do know.<br /><br />Rohan is eventually kidnapped by Ianthe, Roelstra's oldest daughter. Roelstra, despite his mistresses, has not been able to get a son, and Ianthe wants to conceive one with Rohan. Before he marries Sioned, she sneaks into his tent and he realizes while groping her that she's not Sioned and kicks her out. This time, Ianthe drugs him and convinces him that Sioned has come to rescue him, and succeeds in doing the deed with him, hoping that he has gotten her pregnant. Then Rohan wakes up, is furious and starts beating her, and then rapes Ianthe. Meanwhile, Sioned has gone to rescue him, been put in the dungeon by Ianthe, and been raped by her men. Rohan and Sioned are allowed to leave because hey, Ianthe got what she wanted, and they hide in a cave when their horses get away. Sioned spurns Rohan's advances so he gets mad at her, and then all of a sudden, a few chapters later they're fine and lusting after each other like always. Ianthe gives birth to Rohan's son and Sioned steals him, killing Ianthe, intending to raise the boy as their own. Nevermind everyone in the kingdom could see she wasn't pregnant and is probably wondering where the kid came from.<br /><br />Dragon Prince is nearly 600 pages long, and during the last 100 pages, Rawn kept interrupting the action with long chapters full of strategy and soliloquy by secondary characters. That was fine during the first half, but not during the height of the action. I actually skipped around until I found the parts where the action continued and ignored the political ramblings in between. I still understand what happened at the end of the book, so it obviously wasn't that important. <br /><br />All in all, this book was okay. The action, basic structure of the plot, and the world-building were great, but the characterization sucked big time. There are more books in the series, and I won't be reading them. Too bad I bought this at Barnes &amp; Noble instead of getting it from the library.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4121924579963675676" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_270981808" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/270981808" />
    <a title="Stefan Yates" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7590340-stefan-yates"><img alt="Stefan Yates" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328116275p2/7590340.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/270981808?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stefan Yates" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stefan Yates" href="/user/show/7590340-stefan-yates">Stefan Yates</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7590340-stefan-yates?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer270981808" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11616749414940848752">The Dragon Prince is the story about a young prince who is unexpectedly thrown into the seat of power at a very young age. Throughout the story, Rohan struggles with balancing his ideals for peacefully ruling his desert kingdom and the unavoidable need to wage war against those who would threaten that peace. As much as it is about Rohan, it is equally about his wife, Sioned. She is a magic user, called a SunRunner, who's considerable powers are forbidden to be used to kill. However, as a princes</span>
  <span id="freeText11616749414940848752" style="display:none">The Dragon Prince is the story about a young prince who is unexpectedly thrown into the seat of power at a very young age. Throughout the story, Rohan struggles with balancing his ideals for peacefully ruling his desert kingdom and the unavoidable need to wage war against those who would threaten that peace. As much as it is about Rohan, it is equally about his wife, Sioned. She is a magic user, called a SunRunner, who's considerable powers are forbidden to be used to kill. However, as a princess, she must struggle with her own inner demons and the demands to use her powers against her oaths in order to aide and protect her husband.<br /><br />I found this to be an interesting novel written in a style that I'm not entirely used to reading. There is a healthy dose of action and war that I expect in a fantasy novel along with some political intrigue involving the new prince coming to power and working to institute his own ideals. Along with this, there is a lot of emphasis placed upon the developing relationship between Rohan and Sioned. This adds a nice depth to the novel, although at times it gets dangerously close to treading into romance novel territory!! Wink<br /><br />I think that this is one of the rare fantasy novels that will appeal to male and female readers almost equally.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11616749414940848752" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_504391672" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/504391672" />
    <a title="Justin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15431237-justin"><img alt="Justin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1463421725p2/15431237.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/504391672?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Justin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Justin" href="/user/show/15431237-justin">Justin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15431237-justin?shelf=g_fantasy">g_fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15431237-justin?shelf=meta_top_fivepercent">meta_top_fivepercent</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15431237-justin?shelf=read_2017">read_2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15431237-justin?shelf=format_available">format_available</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15431237-justin?shelf=format_owned_phys">format_owned_phys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15431237-justin?shelf=g_fantasy_epic">g_fantasy_epic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15431237-justin?shelf=format_owned_ebook">format_owned_ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15431237-justin?shelf=read_2014">read_2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15431237-justin?shelf=g_fantasy_grimdark">g_fantasy_grimdark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15431237-justin?shelf=g_fantasy_romance">g_fantasy_romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer504391672" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6578385752364375803">Dragon Prince is quite different from most of my favorite series, but it's stuck with me for over 20 years as a cut above most things that I've read. It is far less action-focused than lots of fantasy, instead focusing more on politics, relationships, the nature of leadership, power, and the value of questioning norms.<br/><br/>Unlike most 'political' fantasy this one still has quite a bit of excitement and action as well. Unlike many 'relationship' focused stories this one highlights the fact that all of</span>
  <span id="freeText6578385752364375803" style="display:none">Dragon Prince is quite different from most of my favorite series, but it's stuck with me for over 20 years as a cut above most things that I've read. It is far less action-focused than lots of fantasy, instead focusing more on politics, relationships, the nature of leadership, power, and the value of questioning norms.<br /><br />Unlike most 'political' fantasy this one still has quite a bit of excitement and action as well. Unlike many 'relationship' focused stories this one highlights the fact that all of them carry imperfections and clashes. The series as a whole also taught me at a young age that there are many different forms of love, family, and friendship. Despite all this it is never really preachy and never really boring.<br /><br />It was one of the first 'rules based' magic systems I ever encountered, having numerous restrictions but still carrying with it a sense of amazement. It also flirted with grim dark well before that was a thing and is not afraid to kill off numerous ancillary and even main characters as the series continues.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6578385752364375803" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5640345081493218096">I'm giving this book a 5 star rating but you must understand I read this book a long time ago and in my mind it has always been 'The Book'.   <span id="freeText5640345081493218096" style="display:none">I'm giving this book a 5 star rating but you must understand I read this book a long time ago and in my mind it has always been 'The Book'. Melanie's world was so rich, alive and beautiful - even her 'bad guys'. I realize that is a tad idealistic but I loved it. I loved the way she described her characters, as if each of them was dear to her. Everything in that book felt loved. <br />It is the book that first first made me want to create worlds and characters of my own. I'd read fantasy and sci-fi books before but none touched me the way this one did. It was also my first glimpse into the combining of romance between the MCs in fantasy. I was hooked - I went out, got all the books in the series (both of them) and read them all back to back. <br />PS: I also confess I'm a cover tramp and the main reason I picked this book up is my love of Michael Whelan's artwork. Sue me.</span>

<div id="review_2822122249" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2822122249" />
    <a title="John Adams" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/58175327-john-adams"><img alt="John Adams" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1496479523p2/58175327.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2822122249?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="John Adams" class="user" itemprop="url" name="John Adams" href="/user/show/58175327-john-adams">John Adams</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/58175327-john-adams?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2822122249" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2884092072046045993">Dragon Prince by Melanie Rawn<br/><br/>I was a teenager in Sixth Form when this book was first published, so in deference to my sensibilities and the author's, let's just say 'we are none of us getting any younger' and pass swiftly on.<br/><br/>This is straight up fantasy romance of the best kind. There are battle scenes, but later, much later. In the meantime, plenty of the nigh on 600 pages (a standard length in this subgenre) are devoted to the blossoming relationship between Sunrunner Witch Sioned and the new p</span>
  <span id="freeText2884092072046045993" style="display:none">Dragon Prince by Melanie Rawn<br /><br />I was a teenager in Sixth Form when this book was first published, so in deference to my sensibilities and the author's, let's just say 'we are none of us getting any younger' and pass swiftly on.<br /><br />This is straight up fantasy romance of the best kind. There are battle scenes, but later, much later. In the meantime, plenty of the nigh on 600 pages (a standard length in this subgenre) are devoted to the blossoming relationship between Sunrunner Witch Sioned and the new prince of the desert, whose father has just died. Zehava's passing has catapulted Rohan into a new level of responsibility, and he's uncertain about his ability to fill those boots. But he's also keen to put his own stamp on being a ruler, in particular the possibility of a better relationship with the dragons his father was determined to exterminate.<br /><br />Sioned's her own woman, too, as are Rohan's sister Tobin and aunt Andrade, who leads the sunrunner order of which Sioned is a member. The presence of empowered, confident women (young and old) gives this tale of romance a special warmth to it and contrasts pleasingly with the portrayal of controlled, passive feminity exacted by Rohan's archrival, High Prince Roelstra from his family - with dreadful consequences when Roelstra's womenfolk try to break free from his control.<br /><br />This is a tale of two halves - the obstacles in the way of Sioned's match with Rohan and then the consequences of her infertility six years later. I found the jump a bit of a shock, but once you lean into it the leap gives plenty of fresh impetus to an almost totally separate story in part two. And the action there leads nicely into the rest of the series, since this is just book one.<br /><br />As in any fantasy tale, the layering of detail upon detail to establish the everyday lives and heritage of the various kingdoms is key, and this is done convincingly here. Particularly deft is the portrayal of Sioned's gifts as sunrunner, coupled with the romantic details of life - jewels, flowers, strolls in moonlit gardens and so on - essential to this subgenre.<br /><br />The only drawback I felt was that Roelstra's side were almost irredeemably villainous, whereas Rohan's were almost too good - but there's every sign that a weakening of that dichotomy will occur in subsequent books, and it didn't significantly detract from my enjoyment of one of my favourite books of fantasy romance.<br /><br />Enjoy!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2884092072046045993" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780886774509" href="/book/show/760754.Dragon_Prince">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11078100-amanda-r?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11078100-amanda-r?shelf=fantasy-sci-fi">fantasy-sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11078100-amanda-r?shelf=old-friends">old-friends</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11078100-amanda-r?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer677656390" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12583080998248183460">When I was 15 and going through a very hard time, a girl I worked with handed me three tattered paperback books and told me that they would help me to feel better. She then cautioned me that I couldn't keep them, though - they'd been handed down four times by that point, and the condition was that I had to read them, love them, and then pass them on. <br/><br/>That was 17 years ago, and those books are still sitting on my shelf. Oops. My one defense is that I got the author to sign them (four years after </span>
  <span id="freeText12583080998248183460" style="display:none">When I was 15 and going through a very hard time, a girl I worked with handed me three tattered paperback books and told me that they would help me to feel better. She then cautioned me that I couldn't keep them, though - they'd been handed down four times by that point, and the condition was that I had to read them, love them, and then pass them on. <br /><br />That was 17 years ago, and those books are still sitting on my shelf. Oops. My one defense is that I got the author to sign them (four years after they were originally given to me) and couldn't bear to part with them after that. I have since bought replacement copies, since those were so beat up, and now I just need to cut the autographs out and paste them into the new ones. After I've done that, I'll pass the books along, I swear.<br /><br />And if that isn't a ringing endorsement of the quality of Dragon Prince, I don't know what is. I have loved these stories and characters for more than half my life now. If I read DP now for the first time, I think I would have more nitpicks - after all, Sioned does have definite Mary Sue tendencies, the pacing is a little strange at times, and there are several inconsistencies - but that doesn't really matter now. What matters is that it's a fascinating and compelling story, filled with likable and interesting and very, very real people, and that it provided me with a truly excellent wormhole to disappear into whenever I needed to. I will love these books forever.<br /><br />Update 11/13/16: Yep, still love it.<br /><br />Update 9/12/19: THIS BOOK SUCKS no obviously I still love it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12583080998248183460" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12810390261368547843">I honestly thought that, rereading this for the first time in about 15 years, I'd have more trouble with some of the cheesier bits, but honestly? I still adore it. Cheese included. I love this world. I love how coming back to it always feels like coming home, and how encountering these characters is always like reconnecting with old friends. I love the richness of the magic. I love the dragons. My perspective on some of the characters has shifted somewhat (for example, I'm much quicker now to ca</span>
  <span id="freeText12810390261368547843" style="display:none">I honestly thought that, rereading this for the first time in about 15 years, I'd have more trouble with some of the cheesier bits, but honestly? I still adore it. Cheese included. I love this world. I love how coming back to it always feels like coming home, and how encountering these characters is always like reconnecting with old friends. I love the richness of the magic. I love the dragons. My perspective on some of the characters has shifted somewhat (for example, I'm much quicker now to call Rohan and Sioned out on some of their more hypocritical moves, and I have a LOT more sympathy for Roelstra's daughters, up to and specifically including Ianthe), but I love that, too - being able to get exasperated and/or sympathising with their flaws, in some new ways now that I didn't relate to before. Can't wait to dive into Star Scroll!</span>

<div id="review_160421025" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/160421025" />
    <a title="Ken Badertscher" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5179711-ken-badertscher"><img alt="Ken Badertscher" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442483273p2/5179711.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/160421025?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ken Badertscher" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ken Badertscher" href="/user/show/5179711-ken-badertscher">Ken Badertscher</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5179711-ken-badertscher?shelf=2011">2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer160421025" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2332156638631237695">Romantasy or Fantamance?<br/><br/>Dragon Prince, Melanie Rawnâ€™s first novel, was ahead of the fantasy/romance genre curve in 1988. Rawn decorates an epic fantasy core story with romantic trappings, and it works, most of the time. The early medieval fantasy world of Dragon Prince comes to life in vibrant Sunrunner magical colors. The environments, especially the desert, are depicted in fine detail, capturing the reader with sensuous descriptions. The book has a few minor issues: recurring emotional imagery</span>
  <span id="freeText2332156638631237695" style="display:none">Romantasy or Fantamance?<br /><br />Dragon Prince, Melanie Rawnâ€™s first novel, was ahead of the fantasy/romance genre curve in 1988. Rawn decorates an epic fantasy core story with romantic trappings, and it works, most of the time. The early medieval fantasy world of Dragon Prince comes to life in vibrant Sunrunner magical colors. The environments, especially the desert, are depicted in fine detail, capturing the reader with sensuous descriptions. The book has a few minor issues: recurring emotional imagery and a lack of depth to many of the secondary characters.<br /><br />The main characters are vividly drawn, but the spotlight on them is a bit tight. Everyone seems a little dim compared to Rohan and Sioned, and I suppose that is the novelâ€™s romance side coming to the fore. The reader may get too much inside the head of the characters at some points. A lot of the narrative is filled with the internal monologue and deeply felt emotions of the characters. This tends to give the plot a stuttery feel as conflicts arise, characters ponder, then swoon or glower at each other, then ponder some more, then something else happens.<br /><br />The story is interesting, but not very complex. There is mostly one main thread of plot throughout, though there are many brief branches and callbacks. I think the story could have used a bit of pruning, especially since the general focus is so strong on the main characters. Any time a secondary character comes to the fore, itâ€™s not very rewarding, as they tend to be more sketchy and predictable. The frequent callbacks and rehashing of charactersâ€™ feelings can be distracting, too. Although worded differently and often approached from different angles, some themes are visited repeatedly.<br /><br />Despite these issues, the plotting of the princes and the romance of the main characters is engaging enough to keep the pages turning. Dragon Prince is not for everyone, as it has far more romance and politics than action and adventure. Though few, the action sequences are lively and stimulating. Iâ€™m looking forward to checking out some of Melanie Rawnâ€™s other books set in the Dragon Prince world, as I have a feeling that the later novels may be even better.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2332156638631237695" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_906745800" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/906745800" />
    <a title="Dorian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11385175-dorian"><img alt="Dorian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1344628737p2/11385175.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/906745800?book_show_action=true">Apr 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dorian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dorian" href="/user/show/11385175-dorian">Dorian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11385175-dorian?shelf=other-ebooks">other-ebooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer906745800" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6365916828128228909">I'm not sure how I didn't read this back in the late 80s or early 90s, when it was new and I was reading fairly indiscriminately through the fantasy genre, or as much of it as I could get my hands on. But somehow I didn't.<br/><br/>It bears its age pretty well, I think (unlike, say, Jennifer Roberson's <i>Sword-Dancer</i>, which I found almost unreadable on returning to it recently). Some aspects, mainly the depiction of the romance between the two protagonists, do feel very dated, but most of it still felt very</span>
  <span id="freeText6365916828128228909" style="display:none">I'm not sure how I didn't read this back in the late 80s or early 90s, when it was new and I was reading fairly indiscriminately through the fantasy genre, or as much of it as I could get my hands on. But somehow I didn't.<br /><br />It bears its age pretty well, I think (unlike, say, Jennifer Roberson's <i>Sword-Dancer</i>, which I found almost unreadable on returning to it recently). Some aspects, mainly the depiction of the romance between the two protagonists, do feel very dated, but most of it still felt very fresh.<br /><br />It's basically a coming-of-age story - the coming of age of Rohan, who inherits the Princedom of the Desert at the start of the book; of Sioned, a Sunrunner and Rohan's destined wife; of their world, a conglomerate of Princedoms still mostly ruled by the sword rather than the law, something they aim to change.<br /><br />There's a plethora of interesting and complicated characters, on both the protagonists' and the antagonist's sides. And if the antagonist's motivations are a bit simplistic (power, power and more power), at least both he and those around him are real characters and not just ciphers. It's also pleasing to note that at least as many of the viewpoint characters (of which there are many) are female as male. (And how depressing that 26 years after this book was first published, I still feel the need to note that.)<br /><br />I liked the magic too; the Sunrunners seem to be some kind of religious-based mages - at least they train at the Goddess Keep, though we don't learn anything much about said Goddess. Anyway, they can travel mentally on light to see things far away, or to communicate mentally with each other. And they get really, really sick on water, which makes crossing rivers interesting. And you can prevent them from using their powers by locking them up in the dark.<br /><br />The story does sag a bit in the middle, I thought, and doesn't really pick up again until about the last quarter, but it didn't quite lose my interest.<br /><br />Overall it's a fairly light read, despite some fairly gruesome bits; it doesn't have the gritty feel of some more recent fantasy, which I liked.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6365916828128228909" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Lisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29500755-lisa"><img alt="Lisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1497788399p2/29500755.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1037003070" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14483008027361460349">Melanie Rawn writes epic fantasy that keeps me invested in the story. Her characters are not perfect people, even if they are idealistic--reality won't allow for idealism and they are forced to make decisions and break their own codes of honor time and again. <br/><br/>I enjoyed all of the political maneuvering in this book. That's 90% of the book. Because the entire thing is about power--not wanting it, wanting it, wanting more of it, how it can be a burden, wanting to secure it. But it's also about love</span>
  <span id="freeText14483008027361460349" style="display:none">Melanie Rawn writes epic fantasy that keeps me invested in the story. Her characters are not perfect people, even if they are idealistic--reality won't allow for idealism and they are forced to make decisions and break their own codes of honor time and again. <br /><br />I enjoyed all of the political maneuvering in this book. That's 90% of the book. Because the entire thing is about power--not wanting it, wanting it, wanting more of it, how it can be a burden, wanting to secure it. But it's also about love, and how that has power too. <br /><br />Great book, interesting characters, and I am reminded on this re-read why I loved it so much when I first read it more than 20 years ago.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2593311193655804847">DNF'd this one at 74%. It doesn't deserve any damn stars at all.<br/><br/>I once tried reading this when I was sixteen years old.   <span id="freeText2593311193655804847" style="display:none">DNF'd this one at 74%. It doesn't deserve any damn stars at all.<br /><br />I once tried reading this when I was sixteen years old. From what I could remember of this book, it bored me immensely with the constant politics and heavy focus on everything being driven by sex/libido, and I wound up DNFing it then too. I had recently picked up a secondhand copy for 15Â¢, hoping to give the book a second chance as I'm less likely to be bored to tears as an adult.<br /><br />I could not finish it again, this time because of instances that occur beyond the halfway point of the story. It should come as no shock that my reasons for this stem from the repeated, detailed rape that occurs in the book, and how it gets justified. This absolutely disgusted and appalled me. To think that this is regarded as excellent high fantasy from the point in time of the late 80s, early 90s (and further praised that it was written by a woman) only adds to my disgust. This book deserves no praise whatsoever, and the fact that so few people are willing to admit to any of its flaws (and believe me, there are MANY issues with characterization and logic in the book even before we get to the rape scenes) is extremely disheartening.<br /><br />Got rid of my copy; sold it to Half-Price Books because I didn't have the heart to destroy it or give it to anyone else, and got 50Â¢ back for it. (Hey, at least I made more getting rid of it than I did obtaining the copy.)<br /><br />Do not waste your time with this garbage. I'm disappointed I wasted any of mine on it trying to give it a second chance.</span>

<div id="review_1065934886" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1065934886" />
    <a title="Bridget Coila" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21294696-bridget-coila"><img alt="Bridget Coila" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581304473p2/21294696.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1065934886?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bridget Coila" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bridget Coila" href="/user/show/21294696-bridget-coila">Bridget Coila</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21294696-bridget-coila?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1065934886" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7410512116195817661">For me, this was an ok read...I finished it, but I probably would not read it again and it isn't staying on my shelf (its heading to the used book store next trip that direction.)<br/><br/>At the time it was written, I'm sure it was innovative to have a strong female character as one of the main characters in the book and the departure from "dudes on a quest" style fantasy was a big deal...but in the intervening decades, there are series that are wayyyy more impressive in terms of characterization and plo</span>
  <span id="freeText7410512116195817661" style="display:none">For me, this was an ok read...I finished it, but I probably would not read it again and it isn't staying on my shelf (its heading to the used book store next trip that direction.)<br /><br />At the time it was written, I'm sure it was innovative to have a strong female character as one of the main characters in the book and the departure from "dudes on a quest" style fantasy was a big deal...but in the intervening decades, there are series that are wayyyy more impressive in terms of characterization and plot and general complexity- so this feels kind of boring in many ways.<br /><br />The things that are supposed to be shocking and thought-provoking are mostly just distasteful or ho-hum. Random plot twists that go nowhere (lets kill off half the people in the world with a plague! Now let's forget about the plague and go see who is having babies on the other side of the world...) made me feel like I'd missed some chapters somewhere. The characters are fairly one-dimensional, and they didn't really make me want to follow them through their world.<br />I ended up setting this book aside often while other things caught my interest...then I'd go back to it later because I felt guilty I had not finished it yet and it was sitting there half-read on my side table. So it obviously was unable to really command my attention and interest.<br /><br />If someone happened to have this book on their shelf and loves fantasy, I'd say sure, read it and see if you like it. (Some people absolutely adore this book, for whatever reason...) I wouldn't recommend someone go out and seek it out though.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7410512116195817661" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer102365142" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14748920622782184305">Melanie Rawn's fantasy world full of Sunrunners, Princes and Dragons is one of the most beautiful creations I've read about. The Sunrunners are people who can send their thoughts out over sunlight to communicate or view things over long distances. They learn, inadvertently, that dragons possess this same power. Meanwhile, warring Princes and overly ambitious religious leaders make this story feel more like a political intrigue than a fantasy novel. And just a friendly warning: Rawn isn't afraid </span>
  <span id="freeText14748920622782184305" style="display:none">Melanie Rawn's fantasy world full of Sunrunners, Princes and Dragons is one of the most beautiful creations I've read about. The Sunrunners are people who can send their thoughts out over sunlight to communicate or view things over long distances. They learn, inadvertently, that dragons possess this same power. Meanwhile, warring Princes and overly ambitious religious leaders make this story feel more like a political intrigue than a fantasy novel. And just a friendly warning: Rawn isn't afraid to kill off a character.</span>

<div id="review_11188458" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/11188458" />
    <a title="Tess" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/722677-tess"><img alt="Tess" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1269357532p2/722677.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/11188458?book_show_action=true">Dec 28, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tess" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tess" href="/user/show/722677-tess">Tess</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780886774509" href="/book/show/760754.Dragon_Prince">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/722677-tess?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer11188458" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9519718238801471181">This is a fantastic fantasy series and I am surprised I hadn't found it sooner! The characters and plots are a blend between David Eddings and Anne McCaffrey, but still very unique in many ways.<br/><br/>This takes place in a world where there is no "magic" persay, but there are Sunrunners that can use sunlight and moonlight to view far away places, speak telepathically to eachother, and even create fire and illusions. They are used as messengers, advisors, and spiritual leaders and are held in high regar</span>
  <span id="freeText9519718238801471181" style="display:none">This is a fantastic fantasy series and I am surprised I hadn't found it sooner! The characters and plots are a blend between David Eddings and Anne McCaffrey, but still very unique in many ways.<br /><br />This takes place in a world where there is no "magic" persay, but there are Sunrunners that can use sunlight and moonlight to view far away places, speak telepathically to eachother, and even create fire and illusions. They are used as messengers, advisors, and spiritual leaders and are held in high regard. There are also the Princes, who rule with the power of land and people, and are advised by the sunrunners. And there are dragons.<br />At the time of this book, there is a High Prince who is only concerned with his own ambitions, and a prince-heir Rohan whose Prince father is known for his bravery in battles, and for uniting his subjects. When Rohan becomes Prince in his father's stead, he vows to oust the evil High Prince and rule fairly, lawfully, and justly. Then there is a very talented and skilled Sunrunner, Sioned. She has seen Rohan in a firey vision as her husband and they will be rulers together.<br /><br />This was a great first book, and the first trilogy (Dragon Prince, Star Scroll, and Sunrunner's Fire) are wonderful reads. The second trilogy, Dragon Token, takes place shortly after Sunrunner's Fire. They continue the story when the continent is under attack from foreign invaders.<br /><br />I loved the idea of using sunlight to carry messages, and that the sunrunners are peaceful and exalted people. The laws that Rohan strives to make create interesting politics that are easy to follow.<br /><br />The few down sides I have found is that there are so many names. In several of the books Ms. Rawn has a character glossery in the back, which helps. I was also a little disappointed by the time jumps - sometimes decades go by, and other times many chapters cover just a few days. Her dating system was confusing to me too, until I realized that some chapters took place earlier in time but later in the book to tell what was happening at the same time, different places.<br />Over all the first 2 books were my favorite, and I started disliking some of the main characters in the later 4 books.<br />I still recommend it highly however, and am eager to read other series by Melanie Rawn!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9519718238801471181" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('s0wc0GYVdlEoNoC+sUvhUSfsEKLfmF5E8K9ZJlzsXmrZnkIZu6ChULWcRb0GQOPmagwKKNGaLSKKyiJl+gSpCQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('6TvrVYyfR/s5xaCLhlld+Hc78sSAjD/1h3N0tYuXMAyD6bWcUSqQ+qRvZYgxUl9POtvoTo6OTJP9Fg/2LX/Hbw==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17953393090181187779">Melanie Rawn received a BA in history from Scripps College and worked as a teacher and editor before becoming a writer.<br/><br/>She has been nominated for a Locus award on three separate occasions: in 1989 for Dragon Prince (in the first novel category), in 1994 for Skybowl (in the fantasy novel category), and again in 1995 for Ruins of Ambrai (in the fantasy novel category).<br/><br/></span>
